It is a mind blowing Indian card game. Card games are very popular everywhere. People enjoy them as they just kill boredom.\r\n\r\nIt is also known as MindiKot, Mendhi Coat, Mindi Multiplayer, Dehla Pakad (means \"Collect the tens\") ! \r\n\r\nA slight variation of Mindi is also known as Coat piece. Mindi is considered to be a game for smart people and needs some strategy to win it.\r\n\r\nMindi is designed for four players playing in two partnerships. The game uses a standard 52 card deck. The ranking of the cards in this deck are as follows (from high to low); Ace, King, Queen, Jack, 10, 9, 8, 7, 6, 5, 4, 3, 2. \r\n\r\nThe player who draws the highest card of all would be designated the first dealer. \r\n\r\nThe dealer shuffles the cards and deals the hand. He deals out 13 card hands around the table. \r\n\r\nGame is split into two modes:\r\n\r\nHide Mode- The player to the dealer’s right selects a card placing it to table face down which will be declared as trump suit for that play.\r\n\r\nCut Mode- Play begins without choosing trump suit when the player is unable to follow the suit then whichever he/she chooses becomes the trump of the deal.\r\n\r\nThus, once a trump suit is designated for the hand, the highest card of the trump suit played to the trick wins the trick. If no trump card has been played to the trick, the highest card of the suit led wins the trick. The winner of each trick leads the first card to the next trick. Each captured trick should be kept in a face down pile of cards, gathered by the winner of the trick. \r\n\r\nAfter all 13 tricks have been played the captured cards are then examined to determine the winner of the hand. \r\n\r\nIf one partnership manages to capture three or four of the Tens, they win the hand. If the partnership manages to take all 4 Tens, this is called Mendicot. Winning every trick in the hand is called Fifty-Two card Mendicot.\r\n\r\nThe winner of each hand scores one game point. The first team to score 5 game points is the overall game winner. \r\n\r\nMindi is the traditional, time passing game in India. On top of the downturned cards, an upturned card is dealt on the left-most downturned pile, and downturned cards on the rest until all piles have an upturned card. The piles should look like the figure to the right.\r\n\r\nThe four foundations (light rectangles in the upper right of the figure) are built up by suit from Ace (low in this game) to King, and the tableau piles can be built down by alternate colors, and partial or complete piles can be moved if they are built down by alternate colors also. Any empty piles can be filled with a King or a pile of cards with a King. The aim of the game is to build up a stack of cards starting with 2 and ending with King, all of the same suit. Once this is accomplished, the goal is to move this to a foundation, where the player has previously placed the Ace of that suit. Once the player has done this, they will have \"finished\" that suit, the goal being, of course, to finish all suits, at which time the player would have won. There are different ways of dealing the remainder of the deck:\r\n\r\nTurning three cards at once to the waste, either allowing three passes through the deck or placing no limit on passes through the deck.\r\nTurning three cards at once, reversing the order of each group of three as the cards are dealt.\r\nTurning only one card at a time, but only passing through the deck once.\r\nTurning only one
